; This zone file contains various records used to
; test the maximum size of a DNS responses and behavior
; of clients as they use it.
;
; For more context, please see
; https://www.netmeister.org/blog/dns-size.html
;
; This file is in the public domain.
;
; -Jan Schaumann <jschauma@netmeister.org> / @jschauma

$TTL	300
@	IN	SOA	panix.netmeister.org. jschauma.netmeister.org. (
				2022071636	; Serial
				3600		; Refresh
				300		; Retry
				3600000		; Expire
				300 )		; Minimum
	IN	NS	panix.netmeister.org.

; a response that will yield a truncated response and fail over to TCP
; with ENDS0 payload size 1232, but that will fit into a single UDP packet
; if bind sets
;        edns-udp-size 4096;
;        max-udp-size 4096;
; This may still lead to fragmentation, but will be reassembled
; by the client into a large DNS UDP response.

; 128 A records, leading to truncation and TCP
; since each answer requires:
; - 2 bytes name
; - 2 bytes type
; - 2 bytes class
; - 4 bytes ttl
; - 2 bytes data length
; - 4 bytes IPv4 address
; So 128 * 16 bytes => 2048 bytes answers +
; - 2 bytes length
; - 2 bytes transaction ID
; - 2 bytes flags
; - 2 bytes question
; - 2 bytes # of answer RRs
; - 2 bytes # of auth RRs
; - 2 bytes # of additional RRs;
; - queries:
;   - strlen(query) + 1 (NULL) + 1 byte label count
;   - 2 bytes query type
;   - 2 bytes class
; - 11 bytes additional records (OPT, DNSSEC OK (RFC3225))
128-a	IN	A	127.0.0.0
	IN	A	127.0.0.1
	IN	A	127.0.0.2
	IN	A	127.0.0.3
	IN	A	127.0.0.4
	IN	A	127.0.0.5
	IN	A	127.0.0.6
	IN	A	127.0.0.7
	IN	A	127.0.0.8
	IN	A	127.0.0.9
	IN	A	127.0.0.10
	IN	A	127.0.0.11

; the maximum number of records we can stuff into a response that
; still fits into the TCP limit of 65536:
; 4092 A records * 16 bytes = 65472 bytes
; + len(name)+29 => 65528 bytes
; Note: if DNSSEC is enabled, this won't fit and will fail to return results.

; to illustrate the difference between multiple strings in a single record...
one	IN	TXT	"one" "one"

; ...and multiple records for the same label
two	IN	TXT	"one"
two	IN	TXT	"two"

; a response that fits into exactly 512 bytes, including IP and Ethernet
512-exact	IN	TXT	(
					"xxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxx"
					"xxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxx" )

; a single string can be at most 255 bytes
txt255	IN	TXT	"xxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxx"

; but we can append multiple strings concatenated
txt510	IN	TXT	(
				"xxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxx"
				"xxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxx"
			)

; how many?

				"xxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxx"
				"xxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxx"

			)
